PROPOSED ORDINANCE
Submitting a Proposed Ordinance sponsored by
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., PRESIDENT and WILLIAM R. MORAN, County Commissioners
PROPOSED ORDINANCE

Amending The
Bureau of Human Resources Ordinance
WHEREAS, The County of Cook, Illinois is a home rule unit of local government pursuant to
Article VII, Section 6(a) of the 1970 Illinois Constitution, and pursuant to the authority therein granted,
may exercise any power and perfo rm any function pertaining to its government and affairs; and
WHEREAS, pursuant to its home rule powers the Board of Commissioners of Cook County
adopted an Ordinance creating the Bureau of Human Resources to establish a professional and
progressive merit-based human resources management system and to administer human resource
functions; and
WHEREAS, the Board of Commissioners of Cook County desires that the contributions of
veterans of the United States Armed Forces be recognized and considered for preference in the
examination and selection process for County employment and that the Ordinance be amended to provide
for such preference.

5

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2000
NOW, THEREFORE BE IT ORDAINED by the Board of Commissioners of the County of
Cook, Illinois, as follows:

ARTICLE ONE
Section 4 of the Bureau of Human Resources Ordinance is hereby amended by insertion of the
underlined text in section 4(A)(4) as set forth below:

Section 4.
A.

HUMAN RESOURCE RULES

The Chief of Human Resources shall issue rules to implement the provisions of this Ordinance.
Pri or to the effective date of such rules, the Chief of Human Resources shall give public notice in
one or more newspapers of general circulation, and in no case shall such publication be less than
I 0 days before the effective date of the proposed rule or amendment to the rule. Such public
notice shall include infonnation concerning where the rules can be reviewed and where
comments may be directed. Nothing contained herein shall prohibit the Chief of Human
Resources from giving other appropriate public notice. The rules shall provide for:
( I)

The preparation, maintenance and revision of a position classification plan for all
positions, except those exempted in Section 3 of this Ordinance based upon similarity of
duties perfonned and responsibility assigned, so that the same qualifications may
reasonably be required for and the same schedule of pay may be applied equitably to all
positions in the same class;

(2)

The annual submission of a pay plan to the President;

(3)

The recruitment of persons in the Career Service on the basis of their qualifications.
Whenever it is appropriate, in the judgment of the Chief of Human Resources, a fair and
open lottery procedure may be applied to develop the order of candidates to be considered
for selection. Other selection procedures including, but not limited to interviews,
performance tests, or medical examinations may be applied.

(4)

The establishment of lists of eligibles for appointment and promotion in Career Service,
upon which lists shall be placed the names of successful candidates in order of their relative
excellence in the respective examinations, where such examinations are administered. For
all positions requiring open, competitive written examinations, qualified eligible veterans
shall be entitled to receive five points added to any final adjusted passing score provided
that the veteran has served in the United States Anned Forces on active duty for a pe1iod of
not less than six months of continuous service, was not di shonorably discharged, and
provides documentation confinning status as an eligible veteran . Five additional points
shall be added to a passing score for veterans holding proof of service connected disability
from the United States Veterans Administration or recipients of a purple heart decoration.
Those seeking veterans' preference under this section must submit documentation
confinning their eligibility to the Bureau of Human Resources within five working days of
the examination. The Chief of Human Resources may substitute categorical rankings such
as excellent, well qualified and qualified for numerical rating and establish eligible lists
accordingly. Such rules may provide for lists by area or location, by department or other
agency, for removal of those not available for or refusing employment, for minimum and
maximum duration of such lists, for the addition of names of successful candidates to list
and for such other provisions as may be necessary to provide rapid and satisfactory service
to the operating agencies. The rules may authorize removal of eligibles from lists if those
eligibles fail to furnish evidence of availability upon forms sent to them by the Chief of
Human Resources;

6

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2000
(5)

The certification to an appointing authority the names of a minimum of seven persons, or
all applicants if less than seven apply, (a) with the highest numerical ratings available on
the appropriate eligible list to fill each vacancy, or (b) from the highest ranking group if
the list is by categorical ranking instead of numerical ratings;

(6)

Promotions which shall give appropriate consideration to the applicant' s qualifications,
record of performance and ability;

(7)

Probationary periods after original appointment not to exceed one year. An employee
who completes a probationary period shall have the status of a Career Service employee;

(8)

Probationary periods after promotional appointment not to exceed one year. The rules
may also provide for the restoring of an employee's Career Service status to the class
from which a promotion was made when an employee does not successfully complete a
promotional probationary period or when an employee requests a return to the next lower
rank with the approval of the department head;

(9)

Emergency employment for not more than 60 days with the consent of the Chief of
Human Resources and for provisional employment when there is no appropriate eligible
list available;

( 10)

Keeping records of performance of employees in the Career Service, which performance
records shall be considered in determining salary increments or increases for meritorious
services; as a factor in discharges and transfers. Appropriate performance records will be
maintained for other employees;

( 11)

Layoffs in the Career Service, by reason of lack of funds or work, or abolition of a
position, or material change in duties or organization, and for re-employment of
employees so laid off;

(12)

Implementation and administration of the grievance procedure provided by this
Ordinance;

(13)

The establishment of disciplinary measures such as suspension, demotion in rank or grade,
or discharge. Where employees are subject to a collective bargaining agreement and that
agreement establishes disciplinary or grievances procedures, those procedures control. For
all other Career Service employees, such disciplinary measures shall provide for a
statement of the charges on which discipline is based, together with an explanation of the
evidence supporting the charges and an opportunity for the employee to respond to the
charges in writing before action is taken, appeals after such disciplinary action, and a
hearing on the charges upon request of the employee in case of discharge, demotion or
suspension exceeding 10 work days, consistent with the requirement of due process of law.
The charges and explanation of evidence need not be in any particular form, but must be
sufficient to apprise the employee of the matters on which discipline may be based. The
employee's response must be reviewed by the department head or designee responsible for
making the decision, provided that such designee may be the person who initiated the
charges against the employee. No Career Service employee may be discharged, demoted or
suspended for more than 10 work days unless the statement of charges and any matter in
support are first reviewed by the Chief of Human Resources, before the employee is
notified of such action;

(14)

Development and operations of programs to improve work effectiveness, including
training, education, safety, health, welfare, counseling, recreation and employee relations.

7

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2000
A RT ICLE TWO
This Amendatory Ordinance shall take effect upon passage.

Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commissioner Maldonado, moved that the Proposed Ordinance be
referred to the Committee on Personnel Compliance. (Comm. No. 237896). The motion carried
unanimously.

COMMISSIONERS
PROPOSED RESOLUTIONS
Submitting a Proposed Resolution sponsored by
WI LLIAM R. MORAN, County Commissioner
PROPOSED RESOLUTION
WHEREAS, according to Illinois Statute (65 ILCS 517- 1-47), when a municipality annexes an area of
land the terri tory is automatically zoned as the highest restrictive zoning classification providing
principally for residential use under the municipality's zoning ordinance; and
WHEREAS, this land can be rezoned when it is annexed by the municipality and is automatically
changed if the municipality ' s zoni ng ordinance does not match the County ' s current zoning classification
for the property; and
WHEREAS, the current process of zoning does not consider the best use of the land within the County as
set by the County zoning classification; and
WHEREAS, the County puts fo rth a great deal of effort in order to set the zoning classifications for
County land, however once this land is annexed by a municipality the Coun ty's zoning ordinance and
classification is ignored; and
WHEREAS, the County zoning classification should be respected and considered by the annex ing
municipality in deciding the possible use of the land; and
WHEREAS, at the very least notification should be provided to a County when a portion of that
County's land is being annexed.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners urges the
Illinois General Assembly to review the current legislation regarding annexation and the future use of land
located within Cook County taking special care to include the issues mentioned in this Resolution; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be sent to the Honorable George
H. Ryan, Governor and the Honorable Members of the Illinois General Assembly.

Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commissioner Sutker, moved to suspend the rules so that this matter
may be considered. The motion carried unanimously.

8

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2000
Commissioner Moran, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved that the Proposed Resolution be
referred to the Committee on Zoning and Building. (Comm. No. 237897). The motion carried
unanimously.

* * * * *
Submitting a Proposed Ordinance sponsored by
CAL VIN R . SUTKER and TED LECH OWiCZ, County Commissioners

WHEREAS, Almighty God in His infinite wisdom has called from our midst,
HARRY W. LOCHNER
WHEREAS, Harry Lochner was the loving husband of Grace Steams-Lochner, and
WHEREAS, Harry Lochner was the adoring father of Harry, Tom and Steve, and
WHEREAS, Harry Lochner was the affectionate grandfather of Heather, Holly, Laura, Stephen, Erich
and Kate, and
WHEREAS, Harry Lochner was the great-grandfather of Samuel, and
WHEREAS, Harry Lochner, a lifelong resident of Glencoe, had been active in almost every village
organization, the Glencoe Union Church, and Skokie Country Club. He was recognized as Glencoe's
longest living resident at the Village Centennial Celebration in 1996, and
WHEREAS, Harry Lochner was a pioneer in the field of highway engineering, through the consulting
firm he founded, H. W. Lochner Inc., and
WHEREAS, as a child, Harry Lochner took a variety of odd jobs, delivering papers, starting coal fires in
the neighbors' furnaces and running the daily "Gasoline Alley" comic strip from the cartoonist' s home to
the Northwestern train station for delivery to the Chicago Tribune, and
WHEREAS, Harry Lochner graduated from what is now Central School in Glencoe, New Trier High
School and from the University of Illinois with a degree in civil engineering, and
WHEREAS, Harry Lochner was assistant superintendent of highways for Cook County during the 1930s,
and worked on the development of Chicago's expressway system. He was in charge of planning the
Edens Expressway, and
WHEREAS, Harry Lochner, worked closely with the U.S. Bureau of Public Roads to define how
expressways should be designed, and was involved in innovations such as spiral exit ramps to improve
traffic and origin-destination studies for traffic planning, and
WHEREAS, Harry Lochner started his own engineering firm in 1944, and was responsible for the
original expressway plans for some 30 major cities, including, Jacksonville, Atlanta, Nashville,
.Indianapolis and East Saint Louis. His firm undertook many area projects such as the construction
engineering for O ' Hare Airport and the design of major sections of all of Chicago's expressways. His
finn is a nationally recognized surface transportation consulting engineering finn, and

9

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2000

WHEREAS, Harry Lochner served as a Boy Scout leader before World War II . He was a member and
president of the Glencoe Park District Board and chainnan of the Glencoe Zoning Commission,
responsible for updating the village's zoning laws in the face of rapid subdivision of large estates and
vacant properties in the building boom after World War II. Mr. Lochner also served as a member of the
Glencoe Village Board of Trustees during Glencoe's rapid growth in the 1950s, now
THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners does hereby offer
its deepest condolences and most heartfelt sympathy to the family of Harry Lochner and joins them in
sorrow at this time of loss, and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that this text be spread upon the official proceedings of this Honorable
Body and a copy of same be tendered to the family of Harry Lochner.

This item was WITHDRAWN at the request of the sponsors.

INTERGOVERNMENTAL AGREEMENT RENEW AL
Transmitting a Communication, dated July 13, 2000 from
LACY L. THOMAS, Chief Operating Officer, Cook County Hospital
requesting authorization for the Purchasing Agent to renew Intergovernmental Agreement No. 97-41-242,
as authorized by the County Board on November 7, 1996, with the University of Illinois at Chicago
(UIC), Chicago, Illinois, for the provision of steam services for the Department of Buildings and Grounds
at Cook County Hospital.
In connection with the construction of the new Cook County Hospital, portions of the tunnel system were
demolished. As a result, the supply lines through which steam was supplied to the Administration
Building from the Central Plant were disconnected. This request is to continue the services whereby UIC
provides steam to Cook County Hospital for a unit cost that represents their cost of producing the steam.
Estimated Fiscal Impact: $400,000.00. Contract period: July I , 2000 through June 30, 200 l. (897-449
Account). Requisition No. 08970626.

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved that the request of the Chief
Operating Officer of Cook County Hospital be approved. The motion carried unanimously.

Department of Buildings and Grounds to remove abnormal scaling and chemical build-up on the tubes.

Agreement between the County of Cook and the Village of Glenview
Traffic signal system maintenance and operation
East Lake Avenue at Tall Tree Road
Section: A59-23
Fiscal Impact: not to exceed $2,000.00 (50% reimbursable from Village)
From the Motor Fuel Tax Fund (600-600 Account)

OO-R-427
RESOLUTION
Resolved that the President of the Board of Commissioners of Cook County, Illinois, on behalf of the
County of Cook, is hereby authorized and directed by the Members of said Board, to execute by original
signature or his authorized signature stamp, two (2) copies of an Agreement with the Village of Glenview
to share the cost of maintenance and operation of a traffic signal system presently installed at East Lake
Avenue and Tall Tree Road. (Section: A59-23). It is further agreed that the Village agrees to:
1.

Pay the County fifty (50%) percent of the maintenance charges of the traffic signals within
thirty (30) days of County 's quarterly (3 month) statement of same; and

2.

Assume fifty (50%) percent of the electrical energy charges payable to ComEd in accordance
with the electrical service contract to be entered into with that Company; and

3.

Agrees to use County ' s Electrical Maintenance Contractor for repair of Village OPTICOM
equipment affixed to the referenced traffic signal, enter into an Agreement with said
Contractor for OPTICOM repair and to pay directly to the contractor for said repair costs as
they may occur; and the Highway Department is authorized and directed to return an
executed copy of this Resolution and Agreement to the Village;

August 9, 2000
Commissioner Carr, seconded by Commissioner Hansen, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

ROAD:
FROM:
SECTION:
PLAT NO.:

Devon A venue
Busse Road to Elmhurst Road
98-BI 11 7-04-RS
939

WHEREAS, a public highway, commonly known as Devon Avenue namel y County Highway
B 11 , has been designated and selected by the Cook County Board of Commissioners as a County
Highway, pursuant to its authority under the Illinois Highway Code, 605 ILCS ( 1998) 5/2- 102 and 104
and such designation and selection of the County Highway has been approved by the Illinois Department
of Transportation ("Department"); and
WHEREAS, said County Highway is shown on a map that has been approved by the Department,
a copy of which is on file with the County Clerk of Cook County, Illinois, as well as with the Department,
as provided by statute; and
WHEREAS, the County Board, on February 3, 1998, adopted a Resolution providing for the
improvement and construction of Section: 98-B 1 11 7-04-RS of said County Highway; and
WHEREAS, the Resolution has been approved by the Department; and
WHEREAS, the County Board has adopted a Resolution stating that the public interest requires
the improvement of the above mentioned Section of the County Highway and has requested of the
Department that the County Highway be constructed and improved by law; and
WHEREAS, the Department did consider the desirability and importance of the proposed
improvement and determined that the construction will be practically possible; and

46

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2000
WHEREAS, the Department determined that the improvement will be of public utility and
convenience and after such consideration certified its approval of the proposed improvement to the Cook
County Board of Commissioners; and
WHEREAS, having the Department's approval the Cook County Superintendent of Highways
caused to be prepared proper surveys, maps, plans, specifications and estimates of cost of the proposed
improvement; and
WHEREAS, said plans and surveys require the private property be taken for such improvement
pursuant to authority granted under the 605 ILCS ( 1998) 5/5-80 I ; and
WHEREAS, the private property to be taken consists of real property legally described in the
exhibits submitted herewith.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT, AND IT IS HEREBY RESOLVED, by the Cook County Board of
Commissioners that the Cook County Superintendent of Highways is hereby authorized, empowered and
directed on behalf of the County of Cook to negotiate with the owner(s), and/or any parties of interest in the
property described herein, for the purpose of agreeing to the compensation to be paid for the property; and
IT IS HEREBY FURTHER RESOLVED, that in the event the parties cannot agree on the just
compensation to be paid for taking of the property, the State's Attorney for Cook County, Illinois shall
institute legal proceedings in a court of competent jurisdiction for the purpose of determining the just
compensation to be paid pursuant to the 735 ILCS ( 1998) 5/7-101. Furthermore, the State's Attorney is
authorized and directed to do any and all acts necessary and proper for the acquisition of the property
described herein.
August 9, 2000

Commissioner Carr, seconded by Commissioner Hansen, moved that the Right-of-Way Land Acquisition
Resolution be approved and adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

GRANT AWARD
Transmitting a Communication, dated July 19, 2000 from
DONALD P. O ' CONNELL, Chief Judge, Circuit Court of Cook County
respectfully request that the Cook County Board of Commissioners authorize the Circuit Court of Cook
County to accept a grant in the amount of $20,500.00 from the State of Illinois, Office of the Attorney
General. This grant is funded through the Violent Crime Victims Assistance Act Program and
supplements the County' s current salary for the executive director of the court's Children 's Advocacy
Rooms and the Children's Advocacy Clinic. The court operates six (6) Children' s Advocacy Rooms in
the following court facilities: the Richard J. Daley Center, 50 West Washington Street; the Domestic
Violence Court, 1340 South Michigan A venue; the Juvenile Court, 1100 South Hamilton Avenue; the
Expedited Child Support Center, 32 West Randolph Street; the Family Mediation Unit, Cook County
Administration Building, 69 West Washington Street; and the Sixth Municipal District in south suburban
Markham. The Chi ldren's Advocacy C linic operates in the 1340 South Michigan Avenue court facility.
Funding will be effective upon approval of all parties, for the period July 1, 2000 through June 30, 200 I.
This grant follows County grant number 687, which expires on June 30, 2000.
Estimated Fiscal Impact: None. Grant Award: $20,500.00. Funding period: July 1, 2000 through June
30, 2001.

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved that the request of the Chief
Judge of the Circuit Court of Cook County be approved. The motion carried unanimously.

* * * * *
Transmitting a Communication from
DONALD P. O 'CONNELL, Chief Judge, Circui t Court of Cook County
requesting authorization for the Purchasing Agent to renew Contract No. 99-42-643 with the University
of Illinois at Chicago (UIC), Jane Addams College of Social Work, Chicago, Illinois, fo r professional
consulting services. UIC will assist in evaluating the Court's Domestic Violence Program for
probationers who report to the Social Service Department.

61

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2000
Reason:

The Social Service Department' s Domestic V iolence Program is one of the oldest and largest
of its kind in the United States. More than 1,000 court-referred offenders are supervised
under the program each year . Offenders receive counseling and treatment services as deemed
appropriate by the court and program staff. This contract provides for U IC staff to train
program staff in using offender assessment tools developed in connection wi th the West Side
Domestic Abuse Program, a collaborative effort of UIC, the Social Service Department,
Haymarket Center and other social service organizations. UIC also collects and processes
program data and develops research-based risk factors for noncompliance and recidivism.
UIC was originally selected based upon its previous collaborative efforts with the court and
its experience in developing and implementing assessment instruments. The work will be
directed by Larry Bennett, Ph.D., UIC Jane Addams College of Social Work.

Estimated Fiscal Impact: $60,207 .00 ($15.051.00 (2000) - $45, 156.00 (200 I)). Contract period: August
21 , 2000 through August 20, 200 I. (541-260 Account). Requisition No. 05413032.

Commissioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Steele, moved that the County Purchasing Agent be
authorized to renew the requested contract. The motion carried unanimously.

Requesting authorization to enter into a Memorandum of Understanding between the Judicial Advisory
Council and the State's Attorney 's Office that will govern the administration and management of Project
Reclaim, a Juvenile Accountability Incentive Block Grant initiative funded by the Office of Juvenile
Justice and Delinquency Prevention/U. S. Department of Justice. The Board granted its approval for this
Project and pennission to receive funds for this Grant on June 22, 1999 (New Item # 11).
Project Reclaim is a behavioral and drug rehabilitation program focusing on extremely high risk young
people between the ages of I 0 and 17 years. It focuses on serving three stakeholders in the system; the
juvenile offender, the victim and the community itself. Through programming, holding the juvenile
accountable for the damage he/she has inflicted on the community, and drawing on the strengths of
existing community efforts, Project Reclaim will have a significant impact on the lives of the young
people and the community as a whole.
Project Reclaim will offer its services to a County-wide population.
Estimated Fiscal Impact: $ 109, 798.00. Contract Period: Jul y 11 , 2000 through March 3 1, 200 I.
(205-249 Account).

Commissioner Hansen, seconded by Commissioner Daley, moved that the request of the Executive
Director of the .Judicial Advisory Council be approved. The motion carried unanimously.

by

Re: Emergency Management Assistance Grant
respectfully requests that the above referenced grant be accepted for the Fiscal Year 2001. There are no
personnel costs associated with the grant.
The Illinois Emergency Management Agency (IEMA), as granter, has approved the subject grant for the
grant period of July I, 2000 through June 30, 2001, for a maximum amount of$182,045 .09.

76

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2000
The objective of the Emergency Management Assistance Grant is to provide financial assistance for the
development and continued maintenance of a County emergency management program that effectively
addresses disaster mitigation, preparedness, response and recovery.

CONTRACT
Transmitting a Communication from
DAYID A. BONOMA, Director of Intergovernmental Affairs, State's Attorney's Office
requesting authorization for the Purchasing Agent to enter into a contract with Child's Play Touring
Theatre, Chicago, Illinois, a not for profit educational group located in the City of Chicago. The funds
will be used by Child's Play to develop an anti-violence educational program targeting grade school
children throughout the City and suburban Cook County.
Reason:

We know of no other program in the nation that combines the expertise of experienced
educators with professional actors and a knowledge of how to educate and motivate grade
school-age children to overcome the difficult issues they now face. The program furthers the
policies of Balanced and Restorative Justice that now guide our juvenile justice system by
assisting children to develop competencies in reading and writing, while emphasizing the
need to stay in school, away from drugs, violence and gangs. We funded a pilot program
with this group in 1999, which was a great success.

through September 30, 200 1. (~ 837-260 Account). Requisition No. 02500137.

CONTRACT RENEW AL
Transmitting a Communication from
DAVID A. BON OMA, Director of Intergovernmental Affairs, State' s Attorney' s Office
requesting authorization for the Purchasing Agent to renew a contract with Sylvia J. Dennison, M.D.,
University of Illinois at Chicago, Chicago, Illinois, to continue the "Families-In-Tact" program at the
Juvenile Court facility. This program advocates a comprehensive, family-focused approach to the
treatment of chemical dependency, delinquency and other related issues among families with children
appearing in the Child Protection Division with the goal of keeping families together whenever possible.
The original contract, which included expenses for start-up costs, was in the amount of $670,000.00 with
all funds coming from Fiscal Year 1997 Local Law Enforcement Block Grant (LLEBG) funds. We
request authority to renew the original contract in the amount of $1,000,000.00 for two (2) years using
1998 and 1999 LLEBG funds.
Reason:

We are renewing a contract fo r a highly successful and unique program that has been operated
by the University of Illinois at Chicago. The goals of the program is to keep troubled families
together whenever possible by treating all of the fami ly's related problems simultaneously.
Typically, when a family member is referred to Abuse and Neglect Court, or a child appears in
a juvenile delinquency courtroom, there are numerous, interrelated issues that must be
addressed if a family is to have a realistic opportunity to stay together as a unit, rather than
havi ng children taken out of the home. University of Illinois of Chicago is the only local
agency with the appropriate level of resources, expertise and specialists trained in diverse
aspects of mental health, family counseling and chemical dependency fields to address all of
the potential problems . The program that was funded in 1999 has been a great success.

Estimated Fiscal Impact: None. Grant funded amount: $1 ,000,000.00. Contract period: October I,
1999 through September 30, 200 1. (837-260 Account). Requisition No. 02500138.
Commissioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Steele, moved that the County Purchasing Agent be
authorized to renew the requested contract. The motion carried unanimously.

ROLLING MEADOWS PARK DISTRICT
NO CASH BID REQUEST

Transmitting a Communication, dated July 24, 2000 from
DEBORAH SIMS, Chairman, Tax Delinquency Subcommittee
Submitting a request from
ROGER L. FLOREY, President, Rolling Meadows Park District
Re:

No Cash Bid Program, Lot 5 in the Rolling Meadows Shopping Center Subdivision
Pennanent Index Number 02-36- 100-010-0000 - Volume: 150

The Rolling Meadows Park District does hereby request a no cash bid for the above captioned parcel,
which is located entirely within the territory of the Park District.

87

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2000
The subject parcel is a narrow, unimproved parcel, bounded on the West by Salt Creek and on the East by
a Shopping Center. The parcel's Northern boundary abuts Kimball Hill Park, a public park owned by the
Rolling Meadows Park District. The parcel 's Southern boundary is Kirchoff Road, a main public
thoroughfare.
The Rolling Meadows Park District intends to use the parcel for public access to Kimball Hill Park from
Kirchoff Road and for additional, open park land for the use and enjoyment of the public. We are
enclosing the following:
1.

2.
3.
4.

Certified Resolution fonnally requesting the no cash bid process.
Current title search (commitment) from Chicago Title Insurance Company.
Sidwell Tax Map.
Photographs of parcel.

The primary benefit to the Park District will be the direct access to Kimball Hill Park from Kirchoff
Road. Presently access is through the parking lot of the adjacent Shopping Center. The secondary benefit
is the addition of more land to Kimball Hill Park.
Rolling Meadows Park District affinns that it has retained Bruno W. Tabis, Jr., of Schwartz & Freeman,
401 North Michigan Avenue, # 1900, Chicago, Illinois to obtain the tax deed and will bear all legal and
other costs associated with acquisition of the parcel. The Rolling Meadows Park District further agrees
that it will submit to the Cook County Office of Economic Development an annual report on the status of
the captioned property for five (5) years or until development is completed.

Commissioner Sims, seconded by Commissioner Schumann, moved that the communication be referred to
the Finance Tax Delinquency Subcommittee. (Comm. No. 237895). The motion carried unanimously.

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2000
Chairman Daley asked a representative of the Bureau of Health Services to address the issue of overtime.
Alvin Holley, Chief Financial Officer, Bureau of Health Services, stated the reason for the increase in
overtime is because of nursing and radiology vacancies.
Chainnan Daley asked how the shifts operate?
Mr. Holley responded that it is very difficult to schedule nurses to work the third shift, which causes the
Bureau to recruit nurses for this shift.
Chainnan Daley asked what is the maximum amount of time an individual nurse can work?
Mr. Holley responded that the maximum for nurses is a double shift.
Commissioner Lechowicz stated that other hospitals, including the private sector, are faced with a
shortage of registered nurses. It is not unusual that registered nurses work two shifts.
At the July 11 , 2000 Board Meeting, Commissioner Hansen requested that the Bureau of Health Services
provide revenue and expense figures by ambulatory clinic. He asked the status of the request.
Mr. Holley responded that the request is in progress.
Commissioner Silvestri echoed Commissioner Lechowicz's statement and asked if the County has had a
problem recruiting nurses to fill vacancies within budgetary limitations.
Mr. Holley responded in the affirmative and noted there is difficulty obtaining nurses from the registry.
He stated that registries do not always have the personnel to send to the hospital.
Commissioner Silvestri asked if the County offers wages comparable to private industry?
Mr. Holley responded that the wages are comparable to private industry, but because of the economy,
nurses are going into other professions.
Commissioner Silvestri asked if the County is advertising the benefits that come with employment at
County hospitals, as opposed to working in private facilities?
Mr. Holley responded in the affirmative, but noted that recruitment is difficult.
Commissioner Silvestri referred to the Ambulance and Patient Transportation Service account, 2 I 3. He
asked if this transfer will last throughout the fiscal year or if it is in anticipation of future transfers?
Mr. Holley answered that the funds will last until the end of the year.
Commissioner Silvestri asked why there is a deficit in the Ambulance and Patient Transportation Service
account?
Mr. Holley stated the utilization of the number of patients increased more than what was projected in the
beginning of the fiscal year.
Commissioner Silvestri asked what was the total ambulance service budget?

115

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2000
Mr. Holley responded that he would get back to the Finance Committee with the amount.
Commissioner Moran asked if Cook County Hospital has 12-hour shifts for registered nurses?
Mr. Holley answered that currently Cook County Hospital does have 12-hour shifts.
Commissioner Moreno inquired if the workload in nursing justifies the cost of overtime?
Mr. Holley responded that it is incumbent upon all senior administrators to pre-approve all the overtime
and make sure the overtime is needed.
Commissioner Moreno asked if there will be continued overtime increases after completion of the new
Cook County Hospital?
Mr. Holley projected a reduction in the number of staff needed with the new Cook County Hospital.
Commissioner Maldonado asked what outreach strategies are utilized by the Bureau of Health Services in
recruiting nurses?
Mr. Holley replied that ads are placed in newspapers, and recruitment acti vities are conducted at
universities and job fai rs.
Commissioner Maldonado asked if the recruitment efforts extend out of state?
Mr. Holley answered in the affinnative, but not on a monthly basis. He stated that when there are job
fairs or conferences held out of state, Cook County attends and advertises the benefits of working for the
County.
Commissioner Maldonado expressed his concern that the traditional strategies utilized in the past are not
effective and urged annual visits to other states where there is a surplus of nurses for recruitment in Cook
County.
Commissioner Maldonado asked if Cennak Hospital employees are required to pursue their education in
the same field in which they are employed when utilizing "employee tui tion refund"?
Mr. Holley stated there are provisions in the collective bargaining agreements wherein the County must
provide tuition reimbursement, particularly for nurses.
Chairman Daley asked if there is a requirement regarding the number of years nurses who benefit from
tuition assistance must serve the Bureau of Health Services?
Mr. Holley answered there is no stipulation in the collective bargaining agreement that nurses have to
remain with the Bureau of Health Services for a certain amount of time.

Commissioner Carr moved approval of the transfer of funds request for the Bureau of Health
Services, as amended. Seconded by Commissioner Lechowicz, the motion carried.

Chairman Daley stated that the transfer requests in accounts 214 (Armored Car Service), 242 (Surveys,
Operations and Reports), and 246 (Imaging of Records), are necessitated by delays in processing vendor
bills, and by lapsed purchases from 1999 being carried over to 2000. He asked a representative from the
Recorder's Office to explain.
Geni Johnson acknowledged that payments were taken from the 2000 budget, not the 1999.
Chairman Daley indicated that a more detailed explanation of these bookkeeping errors and accounting
deficiencies would be required by the Finance Committee.
Chairman Daley asked if there was an increase in travel? He further inquired what meetings were held,
the location of the meetings, who attended and why.
Ms. Johnson responded that the increases were due to seminars attended by the Recorder, Chief Recorder,
Deputy Recorder and two attorneys.
Chairman Daley asked Ms. Johnson to provide the information in writing. (See Submitted #2)
Commissioner Lechowicz asked Ms. Johnson to provide to the Committee, in writing, a detailed
explanation of the transfer request regarding the salaries and wages of temporary employees in the 527130 Account. He asked to include what the status is of the deregistration and if temporary employees will
be included in next year's budget as full time positions. Commissioner Lechowicz also asked if regarding
computer equipment, monies will be taken out of FY 1999 or FY 2000 527-579 Account to cover the
negative balance.

Commissioner Collins moved approval of the transfer of funds request for the Recorder of Deeds
Office. Seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, the motion carried.

Commissioner Sutker referred to a $1,000,000 transfer to the Department of Corrections Food Service
Account (223) that indicates the request is within the contract provisions. The Commissioner asked the
reason for the transfer?

119

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2000
James Lee, representative of the Sherifrs Office, responded the number of meals are calculated by the
number of inmates. There are 10,000 inmates eating three meals daily, for a total of up to 30,000 meals
per day. The Sheriffs Department is budgeting for a lower number this year. The Department will cut
back in the beginning of the year on a number of items, with this being one of them.
Commissioner Lechowicz inquired who takes the head count on the daily food outlay? He also asked if
an audit is conducted.
Mr. Lee stated the Sherifrs personnel conduct a daily head count for meals. He also stated that the
figures are audited.
Commissioner Maldonado referred to Account 211-445, Operation of Automotive Equipment, and
inquired if the $650,000 transfer is justified by the recent gasoline price increases?
Jack Kelly, Chief Financial Officer, Sheriffs Office, indicated for 1999 the average gasoline cost was
$1.25 per gallon. For the first 6 months of this year, the average was $1.69, and for the month of June the
average was $2.00.
Commissioner Maldonado asked Mr. Kelly to project how much of an increase he anticipates for the
remainder of the year?
Mr. Kelly speculated perhaps a ten to fifteen cent decrease per gallon.
Commissioner Maldonado referred to line item 211-186, Training Programs for Staff Personnel. He
asked if the training for officers is included in the Administrative and Supportive Services department or
is it in the 230 (Court Services) or 239 (Department of Corrections) departments?
Mr. Kelly responded that the funds are taken from the Administrative and Support Services department,
21 1- 186 for training of all officers.

Commissioner Sutker moved approval of the transfer of funds request for the Sheriff's Office.
Seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, the motion carried.

Your Committee has considered the following communication from the Cook County Board to authorize
a third party lien.
Your Committee, concurring in said request, recommends that authorization of the third party lien be

237506

DOMINIC A VILA, Sheriffs Police Officer
Date of Injury: December 1, 1994
Case Number: 95-WC-9332 (96-L-2051)
Amount of Recovery: $1,007.33
On December I, 1994, Dominic Avila, a Sheriff's Police Officer was injured when his
vehicle was struck from behind, and as a result he injured his back (lumbar sprain and
degenerative disk disease at L3-S I).
Cook County paid Workers' Compensation benefits as follows: $3,408.42 in temporary total
disability benefits, $4,084.36 in medical benefits, and $ 11 ,964.20 for pennanent partial
disability for a total of $19,456.98. Pursuant to the 11linois Workers' Compensation Act, the
County is entitled to recover 75% of its lien, or $14,592.73.
The case was tried and the jury awarded $2,014.67. The County has agreed to accept Yi of
the net award after costs or $1,007.33 of the settlement proceeds. This means the County
would reduce its lien by $13,585.40.
The Finance Subcommittee on Industrial Claims approved the reduction of the County's lien
on July 13, 2000. Therefore, we request Board approval of the lien reduction reflecting a net
recovery of$1 ,007.33.
Lien Recovery:
Lien Waiver:

$ 1,007.33
$13,585.40

COMMISSIONER SCHUMANN, SECONDED BY COMMISSIONER SUTKER, MOVED
APPROVAL OF THE THIRD PARTY LIEN. THE MOTION CARRIED.

237252

COOK COUNTY HOSPITAL, by Lacy L. Thomas, Chief Operating Officer. Transmitting a
Communication, dated July 7, 2000:
Re: Cook County Hospital Corporate Bylaws
l submit for approval by the Board of Commissioners revised Corporate Bylaws for Cook
County Hospital.
Although the Corporate Bylaws have from time to time been reviewed, they were last revised
in 1987. The proposed revision updates the Corporate Bylaws to reflect changes in state
regulations and standards of the Joint Commission on Accreditation of Health Care
Organizations. In addition, the Cook County Board revises the Corporate Bylaws to reflect the
adoption of the Bureau of Health Services Ordinance. The Joint Commission on Accreditation
of Hospitals will next survey Cook County Hospital later this year in November.

*Referred to the Health and Hospital Committee on 7/11/00.
Commissioner Hansen moved approval of the Cook County Hospital Corporate Bylaws. Seconded
by Commissioner Daley, the motion carried.
Commissioner Hansen moved approval of the four amendments.
Daley, the motion carried.

Seconded by Commissioner

Commissioner Hansen asked Assistant State's Attorney Elizabeth Reidy to give brief comments
regarding the amendments.
Ms. Reidy explained that the amendments are marked and the underline in the text indicates that it is a
recommended addition, and a strike-through it means a recommended deletion.
Amendment to Article 1, Offices, Purpose and Powers, Section 1. Office, of the June 2000 draft: Cook
County Hospital, a public hospital established pursuant to the laws of the State of Illinois, is operated and
administered by the Cook County Board of Commissioners (hereinafter "Board"), through its Bureau of
Health Services, to serve as a general public hospital providing care to patients regardless of their ability
to pay, including the medically indigent.
Amendment to Article III, Committees of the Board, Section 2. Special Committees or Subcommittees,
of the June 2000 draft: Special Committees or Subcommittees shall be appointed ey the PresieeAt ef the
Beare er by the Chairmafl ef a staAeiAg eemmittee ef the Beare as may be previeee iA pursuant to Board
Rules.

224

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2000
Amendment to Article VII, Quality of Professional Services, Section 3, Joint Conference Committee, of
the June 2000 draft: The duties of the Joint Conference Committee shall include, but not be limited to:
... considering and approving recommending approval by the Board of plans for the Hospital's response to
and protection and care of patients and others at the time of internal and external disasters; ...
The final amendment is to the June 2000 Draft Cook County Hospital Corporate Bylaws: Proposed
Amendment to the June 2000 Draft Cook County Hospital Bylaws changing the title from "Cook County
Hospital Corporate Bylaws" to "Cook County Bureau of Health Servi ces Corporate Bylaws" and adding
Oak Forest Hospital of Cook County, Provident Hospital of Cook County and the Cook County
Ambulatory and Community Health Network as well as the appropriate amendments necessary to
effectuate this change.
Commissioner Daley asked if Cermak Hospital is included in the amendments?
Elizabeth Reidy stated that Cennak Hospital is considered a department of Cook County Hospital and is
included.
Commissioner Lechowicz asked if all outlying county health facilities are included in the National Joint
Accreditation of Cook County Hospital?
Elizabeth Reidy responded that the JCAH separately surveys each of the county's three hospitals because
they are separately licensed. Ms. Reidy said that JCAH requires Bylaws be in place that set forth the
governance, operating structure and corporate structure. She continued by saying if these Bylaws are
amended, as proposed, each of the hospitals would have Corporate Bylaws that could be turned over to
the JCAH. Ms. Reidy further stated that this was the reason why the Bureau asked to include Ambulatory
Care in the Bylaws.
Commissioner Sims asked if these Bylaws encompass all the County's hospitals?
Elizabeth Reidy responded affinnatively. She said there would be one set of Corporate Bylaws for the
entire Bureau of Health that would include four of the affiliates, the three hospitals and ambulatory care.
Ms. Reidy further stated that if the fourth amendment is approved, the State' s Attorney's Office would
draft the changes that were required and the only thing that might change would be for the "purposes" of
the hospital, where now there is only the purpose of Cook County Hospital so a separate paragraph would
be added describing Oak Forest, Provident and Ambulatory Care. The officers would remain the same in
the hospital s but the ambulatory might be a little different so it would be separated out and a copy would
be given to the commissioners before the August 9, 2000 Board Meeting with all the changes that would
be required along with the technical changes that are required for amendment four.

Commissioner Hansen, seconded by Commissioner Daley, moved to approve Communication No.
237252, as amended. The motion carried.
Commissioner Hansen voted Present on Section V "sexual orientation".

225

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2000
COOK COUNTY BUREAU OF HEALTH SERVICES
CORPORATE BYLAWS
ARTICLE I.
BUREAU AFFILIATES
Section 1. Bureau Affiliates
The Cook County Bureau of Health Services (hereinafter " Bureau") is composed of multi ple
affiliates including three separately licensed hospitals. These hospitals are Cook County Hospital, Oak
Forest Hospital of Cook County (hereinafter "Oak Forest Hospital") and Provident Hospital of Cook
County (hereinafter " Provident Hospital") (hereinafter collectively referred to as "Affiliate Hospitals").
The Bureau affiliates also include the Cook County Ambulatory and Community Health Network
(hereinafter "ACHN").
ARTICLE II.
OFFICES, PURPOSE AND POWERS
Section 1. Offices
(a) Cook County Hospital
Cook County Hospital, a public hospital established pursuant to the laws of the State of Illinois, is
operated and administered by the Cook County Board of Commissioners (hereinafter " Board"), through
its Bureau of Health Services, to serve as a general public hospital providing care to patients regardless of
their ability to pay, including the medically indigent. Cook County Hospital is located at 1835 W.
Hamson Street in the City of Chicago, County of Cook, State of Illinois. The principal office for the
County of Cook is I 18 N. Clark Street in the City of Chicago, County of Cook, State of Illinois.
(b) Oak Forest Hospital
Oak Forest Hospital, a public hospital established pursuant to the laws of the State of Illinois, is
operated and administered by the Board, through its Bureau of Health Services, to serve as a health care
center devoted to the diagnosis, treatment, rehabilitation and long-tenn care of persons suffering from
chronic illnesses and physical disabilities regardless of their ability to pay, including the medically
indigent. Oak Forest Hospital is located at 15900 South Cicero Avenue in the City of Oak Forest, County
of Cook, State of Illinois. The principal office for the County of Cook is 11 8 N. Clark Street in the City
of Chicago, County of Cook, State of Illinois.
(c) Provident Hospital

Provident Hospital, a public hospital established pursuant to the laws of the State of Illinois, is
operated and administered by the Board, through its Bureau of Health Services, to serve as a community
teaching hospital providing care to patients regardless of their ability to pay, including the medically
indigent. Provident Hospital is located at 500 East 5 1st Street in the City of Chicago, County of Cook,
State of Illinois. The principal office for the County of Cook is 11 8 N. Clark Street in the City of
Chicago, County of Cook, State of Illinois.

226

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2000
(d) ACHN

The ACHN, a public network of hospital-based and community-based outpatient health centers
throughout Chicago and Suburban Cook County, is operated and administered by the Board, through its
Bureau of Health Services, to provide outpatient and community health services to patients regardless of
their ability to pay, including the medically indigent. The principal office for the ACHN is located at
1835 W. Harrison Street in the City of Chicago, County of Cook, State of Illinois. The principal office
for the County of Cook is 118 N. Clark Street in the City of Chicago, County of Cook, State of Illinois.

Section 2. Purpose and Powers
The management, control and operation of the affairs and properties of the Affiliate Hospitals and
the ACHN shall be as provided by the Board herein and as in such Ordinances and Resolutions as
approved by the Board. The powers and authority of the Board regarding the affairs of the Affiliate
Hospitals are provided for in 55 ILCS 5/5-37001 et seq., Cook County Ordinances and Resolutions and in
these Corporate Bylaws.
(a)

The purpose of Cook County Hospital shall be:

(I)

To operate and maintain a general public hospital and other health care facilities and
programs for the care of the residents of Cook County and to operate departments
providing services necessary for and incident to the care of the residents of Cook County,
regardless of their ability to pay including the medically indigent.

(2)

To conduct and maintain educational programs relating to the rendering of care to the sick
and injured as deemed appropriate in light of the Hospital's facilities, personnel and funds.

(3)

To promote and conduct biomedical research to improve the overall health of and
delivery of services to the Hospital's patient population.

(4)

To participate, as deemed appropriate, in activities designed to promote the general health
of the residents of Cook County.

(b)

The purpose of Oak Forest Hospital shall be:

(1)

To operate and maintain a public hospital and programs for the care of the residents of
Cook County requiring long term care services, regardless of their ability to pay,
including the medically indigent.

(2)

To promote optimal functioning and independence of its patient population.

(3)

To coordinate health services with the Bureau emphasizing rehabilitation and ventilator
services and to be effective stewards of public resources, recognizing and serving
community needs.

(4)

To participate, as deemed appropriate, in activities designed to improve the health status
of the residents of Cook County.

(c)

The purpose of Provident Hospital shall be:

227

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDfNGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2000
(I)

To operate and maintain a community public hospital and programs and services for the
care of the residents of Cook County, regardless of their ability to pay, including the
medically indigent.

(2)

To promote and conduct educational programs relating to the rendering of care to the sick
and injured, as deemed appropriate, in light of the Hospital 's facilities, personnel and funds.

(3)

To conduct biomedical and service-based research to improve the overall health of and
delivery of services to the Hospital 's patient population.

(4)

To participate, as deemed appropriate, in activities designed to improve the health status
of the residents of Cook County.

(d)

The purpose of the ACHN shall be:

(I)

To operate and maintain a system of ambulatory care facilities including communitybased primary health centers and hospital-based outpatient specialty centers for the care
of residents of Cook County regardless of their ability to pay, including the medically
indigent.

(2)

To develop, foster and operate ambulatory care and community health programs and
services that meet the health needs of residents of Cook County in the most effective and
efficient manner.

(3)

To coordinate health services with the Bureau to provide a continuous and
comprehensive health care system that prevents and treats disease, rehabilitates, trains
health care providers, and conducts research.

( 4)

To participate, as deemed appropriate, in activities designed to promote the general health
of the residents of Cook County.

ARTICLE III.
COOK COUNTY BOARD OF COMMISSIONERS
Section 1. Method of Selection
Commissioners of the Board shall be elected by the legal voters of Cook County as provided by
law.

Section 2. Vacancy In Office of Commissioner
If a vacancy occurs in the Office of a Commissioner, said vacancy shall be filled as provided by
law.

Section 3. President
The President of the Board shall be elected by the legal voters of Cook County as provided by
law.

228

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2000
Section 4. Vacancy In Office of President

If a vacancy occurs in the Office of President, said vacancy shall be filled as provided by law.
Section 5. Terms of Office

The terms of office of the Commissioners and the President of the Board shall be as provided by
law.
Section 6. Meetings

The Board shall hold regular meetings as provided by Board Rule. The President shall preside at
all meetings of the Board and generally perform the duties of a presiding officer. Special meetings shall
be held as provided by Board Rule. Other matters regarding the conduct of Board meetings shall be as
provided by law or Rule of the Board.
Section 7. Powers

The affairs of the Affiliate Hospitals and the ACHN shall be managed by the Board which shall
have responsibility for the control and management of the property, funds and operations of the Affiliate
Hospitals and the ACHN and said Board shall have full power and authority to do and perform any and
all acts and functions which are not inconsistent with law. The Board has, as a specific power, the
approval of the bylaws and constitutions of all subsidiary organizations of the Affiliate Hospitals and the
ACHN including the Affiliate Hospital Medical Staffs and auxiliary organizations. The Board also has
the following authority which includes, without limitation, the power:
(a)

To amend these Bylaws.

(b)

To appoint, terminate or modify membership in the Affiliate Hospital Medical Staffs in
accordance with the procedure established in the Medical Staff Bylaws.

(c)

To receive and act upon the budget recommendations and to review and approve
finances, costs and charges, as well as general wage and salary increases or decreases.

(d)

To make, amend, repeal or, where applicable, approve overall policies for the operation
of the Affiliate Hospitals and the ACHN which outline the general goals or acceptable
procedures or which outline a definite course of action to guide and determine present
and/or future conduct and/or decisions consistent with applicable law and regulatory
requirements.

(e)

To approve rules and regulations of the Affiliate Hospital Medical Staffs.
ARTICLE IV.
COMMITTEES OF THE BOARD

Section 1. The Health and Hospitals Committee

Among the standing committees required pursuant to Board Rules, which may be changed only
by appropriate vote of the Board, is the Health and Hospitals Committee.

229

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2000
The Health and Hospitals Committee shall perfonn all duties delegated to it by the Board. The
Health and Hospitals Committee shall be responsible for the review of all aspects of the Bureau's
operations referred to it by the Board and shall report on and recommend policy to the Board.

Section 2. Special Committees or Subcommittees
Special Committees or Subcommittees shall be appointed pursuant to Board Rules.

ARTICLE V.
BUREAU OF HEALTH SERVICES OF COOK COUNTY
The Board established the Bureau of Health Services of Cook County to consolidate the various
departments responsible for the delivery of health services in Cook County. The Bureau includes the
following affiliates: Cermak Health Services of Cook County, Cook County Ambulatory and Community
Health Network, Cook County Department of Public Health, Cook County Hospital, Oak Forest Hospital
of Cook County and Provident Hospital of Cook County. The affiliates of the Bureau may change to
meet the needs of the patient population served by the Bureau.
The Chief of the Bureau is appointed by the President of the Board with the approval of the
Board. The Chief of the Bureau is responsible for the management and direction of the Bureau and of any
other agency, function or matter the President or the Board may assign. The Chief Operating Officer of
each Bureau affiliate shall report directly to the Chief of the Bureau.

ARTICLE VI.
OFFICERS OF THE AFFILIATE HOSPITALS AND THE ACHN
Section 1. Officers
Each Affiliate Hospital and the ACHN shall have a Chief Operating Officer, Medical
Director/Chief Medical Officer and such other officers as the Board shall detennine are necessary or
desirable. Al l officers shall be appointed by the President of the Board with the approval of the Board to
serve at the pleasure of the Board.

Section 2. Chief Operating Officer
The Chief Operating Officer shall serve as the chief administrator of the Affili ate Hospital or of
the ACHN. The Chief Operating Officer shall have the necessary authority and responsibility for the
administration of the day-to-day affairs of the Affiliate Hospital or of the ACHN subject to these Bylaws
and the authority of the Chiefof the Bureau.
Subject to the authority of the Chief of the Bureau, the authority and duties of the Chief Operating
Officer shall include, but not be limited to:
(a)

The presentation of recommendations to the Board relating to the operations and longrange planning of the Affiliate Hospital or of the ACHN and shall carry out the policies
and directives of the Board;

(b)

The preparation of and presentation to the Board of periodic reports on the operation and
condition of the Affiliate Hospital or of the ACHN; and,

230

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2000
(c)

The presentation directly to the Board for approval of all contracts and agreements
relating to purchases and services as required by Cook County Ordinance.

(d)

The general organization and administration of the Affiliate Hospital or of the ACHN and
all its activities and departments subject to the approval of the Board.

(e)

The enforcement of all Corporate Bylaws, County, Bureau and Affiliate Hospital or ACHN
policies, rules, and regulations and the observance by personnel of all applicable laws.

(f)

The preparation and presentation to the President for submission to the Board of
necessary reports with respect to the operation of the Affiliate Hospital or of the ACHN.

(g)

The preparation and presentation to the Board for its approval of an annual budget
recommendation showing expected revenues and expenditures.

(h)

The implementation of all policies established by the Board.

(i)

The selection, supervision, and discharge of employees and the development and
maintenance of personnel policies and practices.

(j)

The maintenance of physical properties in a good and safe state of repair and operating
condition.

(k)

The supervision of business affairs to ensure that funds are collected and expended to the
best possible advantage.

(I)

In conjunction with the Medical Director/Chief Medical Officer and health care
professionals, maintenance of an environment within which care of a standard generally
accepted in the applicable community may be rendered to the patients at all times.

(m)

The preparation and presentation to the Board or its authorized committees of periodic
reports reflecting professional services and financial activities and such special reports as
may be required.

(n)

Attendance at all meetings of the Board and of committees thereof, as required.

(o)

With respect to the Chief Operating Officer of an Affiliate Hospital, service as a liaison
between the Board or any of its committees and the Medical Staff and assisting the
Medical Staff with its organization and administrative responsibilities.

(p)

Preparation of a plan for the achievement of specific objectives and periodically
reviewing and evaluating that plan.

(q)

Representation of the Affiliate Hospital or of the ACHN in its relationships with other
health agencies.

(r)

With respect to the Chief Operating Officer of an Affiliate Hospital, receipt and
transmission of recommendations from the Medical Staff regarding Medical Staff
appointment or reappointment, or the grant or termination of clinical privileges in
accordance with Affiliate Hospital Medical Staff Bylaws.

231

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2000
(s)

With respect to the Chief Operating Officer of an Affiliate Hospital, the granting and
tennination of temporary Medical Staff privileges in accordance with Medical Staff
Bylaws.

(t)

With respect to the Chief Operating Officer of an Affiliate Hospital, imposition of
summary suspension in accordance with Medical Staff Bylaws.

(u)

With respect to the Chief Operating Officer of an Affiliate Hospital, performance of other
duties in accordance with Medical Staff Bylaws.

(v)

Perfonnance of other duties that may be necessary or in the best interest of the Affiliate
Hospital or of the ACHN consistent with the authority granted by the Board.

The Chief Operating Officer shall perform all duties incident to the office of Chief Operating
Officer and such other duties as may be prescribed by the Chief of the Bureau or the Board.

Section 3. Medical Director/Chief Medical Officer
The Medical Director/Chief Medical Officer shall be responsible for the overall medical affairs of
the Affiliate Hospital or of the ACHN and shall report directly to the Chief Operating Officer and, as
requested, to the Board on medical matters.
The duties of the Medical Director/Chief Medical Officer shall include, but not be limited to:
(a)

Directing, coordinating, monitoring and evaluating the medical activities of the Affiliate
Hospital or of the ACHN.

(b)

Participating with Affiliate Hospital Department Chairs (hereinafter "Department
Chairs") or ACHN Health Center Clinical Directors (hereinafter "ACHN Clinical
Directors") in the fonnulation of budget recommendations, goals and objectives, and
reviewing and monitoring the ongoing activities of each Department or ACHN Health
Center in the achievement of its stated goals and objectives.

(c)

Evaluating the administrative and clinical activities of the Department Chairs or ACHN
Clinical Directors.

(d)

Monitoring the quality of medical care by directing and assuring the proper function of
the various quality control programs and committees. Also, with respect to Medical
Directors/Chief Medical Officers of the Affiliate Hospitals, reviewing activities of all
standing and special committees of the Medical Staff and addressing issues raised and
recommendations made by these committees.

(e)

In consultation with medical residency program directors and/or the Department Chairs
or ACHN Clinical Directors, recommending policy, rules and regulations for the house
staff assigned to the Affiliate Hospitals or ACHN, consistent with applicable agreements
and the Accreditation Council for Graduate Medical Education Guidelines. In addition,
monitoring the quality of continuing medical education and faculty development.

(f)

With respect to Medical Directors/Chief Medical Officers of the Affiliate Hospitals,
assuming responsibility for matters pertaining to Affiliate Hospital Medical Staff
membership including, but not limited to, the following:

232

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2000

(g)

1.

Receiving, reviewing and making recommendations on all applications for
appointment to the Affiliate Hospital Medical Staff in accordance with the
Affiliate Hospital Medical Staff Bylaws.

2.

Receiving, reviewing and making recommendations, if appropriate, on
reappointments to the Affiliate Hospital Medical Staff or on modifications or
terminations of clinical privileges in accordance with the Affiliate Hospital
Medical Staff Bylaws.

3.

Attending meetings of the Affiliate Hospital Medical Staff and serving on such
Medical Staff committees as provided for in the Affiliate Hospital Medical Staff
Bylaws.

4.

Assisting the Affiliate Hospital Medical Staff with its organization and
responsibilities and serving as a liaison between the Affiliate Hospital Medical
Staff and administration.

5.

Serving as a liaison between the Affiliate Hospital Medical Staff and the Board
and maintaining communication between the two.

6.

Keeping records of all Affiliate Hospital Medical Staff members and house staff
regarding licensing and other relevant information.

With respect to Chief Medical Officer(s) of the ACHN, assuming responsibility for
matters pertaining to providers permitted to provide health services within ACHN Health
Centers including, but not limited to, the following:
1.

Receiving, reviewing and making recommendations to the Chief Operating
Officer with respect to providers requesting to provide health services within
ACHN Health Centers.

2.

Receiving, reviewing and making recommendations, if appropriate, to the Chief
Operating Officer on requests by providers for clinical privileges within ACHN
Health Centers, including modifications or terminations of such clinical
privileges, to the extent privileges may be required pursuant to ACHN policy.

3.

Directing and assisting the ACHN Clinical Directors in perfonning their
responsibilities and serving as a liaison between the Clinical Directors and
ACHN administration.

4.

Keeping records of all ACHN providers, including house staff, regarding
licensing and other relevant infonnation.

(h)

Participating in all surveys conducted by various accrediting and regulatory bodies such
as the Joint Commission on Accreditation of Healthcare Organizations, the Illinois
Department of Public Health, the United States Department of Health and Human
Services and the medical surgical specialty boards.

(i)

Performing other duties as requested and as directed by the Chief Operating Officer.

233

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2000

ARTICLE VII.
AFFILIATE HOSPITAL MEDICAL STAFFS
Section I. Composition and Appointment
The Board shall appoint a Medical Staff for each Affiliate Hospital composed of such qualified
individuals who hold licenses to practice medicine, osteopathy, podiatry, chiropractic services or dentistry
in the State of Illinois. The Medical Staff of each Affiliate Hospital shall adopt Bylaws and Rules and
Regulations for the government of medical and dental practice in the Hospital. When approved by the
Board, Affiliate Hospital Medical Staff Bylaws and Rules and Regulations shall be binding upon both the
Affiliate Hospital Medical Staff and the Board.

Section 2. Delegation of Authority
The Board, through the Chief of the Bureau, the Chief Operating Officer and the Medical
Director/Chief Medical Officer, shall assign to the Affiliate Hospital Medical Staff the overall
responsibility for the quality of the professional services provided within the Affiliate Hospital facilities
by individuals with clinical privileges. The Affiliate Hospital Medical Staff shall make recommendations
to the Board regarding the appointment, reappointment or modification of Medical Staff appointments
and the granting of clinical privileges in accordance with the Affiliate Hospital Medical Staff Bylaws.
Acknowledging its responsibility for the preservation and improvement of the quality and
efficiency of patient care provided in the Hospital, the Board shall require that the Affiliate Hospital
Medical Staff conduct activities fulfilling said responsibility including:
(a)

Making recommendations regarding the appointment, reappointment, and delineation of
clinical privileges for members of the Affiliate Hospital Medical Staff commensurate
with individual credentials and demonstrated ability and judgment, and the assignment of
patient care responsibilities to other health care professionals consistent with individual
qualification and demonstrated ability.

(b)

Providing continuing professional education, shaped primarily by the needs identified
through review and evaluation activities.

(c)

Implementing utilization review measures based on specific patient needs to assure
prudent use of the Affiliate Hospital's resources.

(d)

On-going monitoring of patient care practice through defined function of the Affiliate
Hospital Medical Staff.

(e)

Conducting retrospective review and evaluation of the quality of patient care through a
valid and reliable patient care evaluation procedure.

(f)

Managing clinical affairs, including enforcement of Affiliate Hospital Medical Staff
Bylaws and Rules and Regulations, clinical policies and consultation requirements.

(g)

Performing such other activities as the Board, the Chief of the Bureau, the Chief
Operating Officer or the Medical Director/Chief Medical Officer may deem necessary for
the preservation and improvement of the quality and efficiency of patient care.

234

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2000

Section 3. Affiliate Hospital Medical Staff Bylaws
Each Affiliate Hospital Medical Staff shall have written bylaws, rules and regulations which are
approved by the Board.

Section 4. Criteria For Appointment And Privileges
In acting on matters of Affiliate Hospital Medical Staff membership status, the Board shall
consider the Affiliate Hospital Medical Staffs and administration's recommendations, the Affiliate
Hospital 's and community's needs, and such other criteria as are set forth in the Affiliate Hospital
Medical Staff Bylaws. In granting and defining the scope of clinical privileges to be exercised by each
Affiliate Hospital Medical Staff member, the Board shall consider the Affiliate Hospita l Medical Staffs
recommendation, the supporting information on which it is based and such criteria as are set forth in the
Affiliate Hospital Medical Staff Bylaws. No aspect of membership status nor specific clinical privileges
shall be limited or extended on the basis of race, color, sex, age, religion, disability, national origin,
ancestry, sexual orientation, marital status, parental status, military discharge status, source of income or
housing status.

ARTICLE VIII.
QUALITY OF PROFESSIONAL SERVICES
Section 1. Board Responsibility
The Board shall be responsible for assuring that all patients presenting to the Affiliate Hospitals
and the ACHN receive quality health care services and for assessing the recommendations of the Chief of
the Bureau, Chief Operating Officers, Medical Directors/Chief Medical Officers, Affiliate Hospital
Medical Staffs and others knowledgeable in the delivery of patient care services. The Board shall assure
that processes are in place enabling it to review and evaluate activities to assess, preserve and improve the
overall quality and efficiency of patient care. The Board, through the Chief Operating Officers, shall
provide such administrative assistance as is reasonably necessary to support and facilitate the
implementation and performance of these review and evaluation activities.

Section 2. Documentation
The Board shall require, receive, consider and act upon the findings and recommendations of the
Chief of the Bureau, Chief Operating Officers, Medical Directors/Chief Medical Officers and Affiliate
Hospital Medical Staffs with regard to their respective responsibilities as set forth in these Bylaws. All
such findings and recommendations shall be in writing, signed by the persons responsible for conducting
the relevant activities and supported and accompanied by reliable documentation upon which the Board
can take infonned action.

Section 3. Joint Conference Committees
Each Affiliate Hospital shall have a Joint Conference Committee which shall be a standing
committee of the Affiliate Hospital. Each Joint Conference Committee shall be composed of: a certain
number of members of the Board as provided in the Affiliate Hospital Medical Staff Bylaws appointed by
the Board' s President; the C hief of the Bureau, if provided for in the Affiliate Hospital Medical Staff
Bylaws; the Chief Operating Officer; the Medical Director/Chief Medical Officer, the President, VicePresident, Secretary, and Treasurer of the Affiliate Hospital Medical Staff; and two members of the
Affiliate Hospital Executive Medical Staff Committee elected by that Committee.
The Chair shall alternate each year between a Commissioner of the Board, selected by the
President of the Board, and the President of the Affiliate Hospital Medical Staff.

235

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2000
The duties of the Joint Conference Committees shall include, but not be limited to: providing a
liaison among the Board, Affiliate Hospital Medical Staff and Affiliate Hospital administration;
conducting itself as a forum for the discussion of matters of policy and practice of a medicaladministrative nature; reviewing Affiliate Hospital compliance with the standards, rules and regulations
of the various accrediting and licensing agencies; considering and recommending approval to the Board
of plans for the Hospital 's response to and protection and care of patients and others at the time of internal
and external disasters; and, assisting in coordinating the Hospital' s plans with those of other health care
facilities and other agencies in the community.

ARTICLE IX.
GENERAL PROVISIONS
Section 1. Auxiliary and Associated Organizations
The Board may authorize the formation of auxiliary and associate organizations to assist in the
fulfillment of the purposes of the Affiliate Hospital or ACHN. Each such organization shall establish its
Bylaws and Rules and Regulations and make amendments thereto which shall be subject to the approval
of the Board and which shall not be inconsistent with these Bylaws, the Affiliate Hospital Medical Staff
Bylaws or the Rules of the Board.

Section 2. Fiscal Year
The fiscal year of the Affiliate Hospital and the ACHN shall be the fiscal year of the County of
Cook which commences on December Ist of each year.

Section 3. Seal
The Seal of the Affiliate Hospital and the ACHN shall be the Seal of the County of Cook.

Section 4. Amendments
These Bylaws may be amended either in whole or in part or repealed by vote of a majority of the
Board.

Vice Chairman Schumann moved to adjourn the meeting, seconded by Commissioner Moran. The
motion carried and the meeting was adjourned.
Respectfully submitted,
COMMITTEE ON HEALTH AND HOSPITALS
JERRY BUTLER, Chairman
