REPORT OF THE COMMITTEE ON VETERANS
July 27, 2000
The Honorable,
The Board of Commissioners of Cook County

ATTENDANCE
Present:

Chairman Moran, Vice Chainnan Hansen, Commissioners Carr, Daley and Quigley (5)

Also Present:

John Houlihan - Superintendent, Veterans Commission

Absent:

Commissioner Butler and Schumann (2)

Ladies and Gentlemen:
Your Committee on Veterans of the Board of Commissioners of Cook County met pursuant to notice on
Thursday, July 27, 2000 at the hour of 2:30 P.M. in the Board Room, Room 569, County Building, 118
North Clark Street, Chicago, Illinois.
Your Committee has considered the following item and upon adoption of this report, the
recommendations are as follows:
237251

SOLDIER FIELD RESOLUTION (PROPOSED RESOLUTION). Submitting a Proposed
Resolution sponsored by William R. Moran, County Commissioner and Co-sponsored by
Gregg Goslin, Carl R. Hansen and Calvin R. Sutker, County Commissioners:
The following is a synopsis.

WHEREAS, plans for creating Soldier Field began in 1919 as a memorial to the soldiers of
the First World War; and
WHEREAS, Soldier Field was opened in 1924 as the Municipal Grant Park Stadium, with
45,000 seats; and
WHEREAS, Soldier Field was dedicated on November 27, 1926 after an Army Navy
football game, ending in a 2 1-21 tie; and
WHEREAS, the Chicago Park District is considering renaming Soldier Field in order to
receive money from a corporate sponsor in order to pay for renovations; and
WHEREAS, Soldier Field is a grand structure with a great history, and is a great landmark
for the City of Chicago and Cook County; and
WHEREAS, the grand structure of Soldier Field is a unique memorial to the Soldiers who
have served the United States of America.

237

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDTNGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2000

NOW, THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners
urges the Chicago Park District to continue to honor the soldiers of the United States of
America by keeping the name Soldier Field as a tribute to the Soldiers of our county as
originally planned in 1919; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be sent to the
Chicago Park District and the City of Chicago.
Commissioner Carr asked if Cook County owns Soldier Field?
Chairman Moran responded that the County does not own Soldier Field.
Commissioner Daley stated that the County would set a precedent not only for the City of Chicago, but
any municipality by approving this resolution. He further stated that the County should review the
resolution and work with the Chicago Park District and the City of Chicago on the issue. Also, he stated
that the Mayor and Park District representatives have indicated that the facility will continue to be named
Soldier Field.
Commissioner Daley stated that he is concerned that if the City and Park District are still in negotiations,
nothing is on the table for discussion. He stated for anything to be renamed within a Park District, an
individual must come to the park and present it to the board, which at this point has not occurred. The
Commissioner stated that he is concerned that no representatives were invited to the Veterans Committee
meeting. Finall y, he said he believes the County Board is in support of retaining the name, Soldier Field.
Vice Chainnan Hansen stated that he is completely in support of the resolution. He stated that the direct
responsibility for the field lies in the hands of the Chicago Park District and it would be well for the County
Board to hear from representatives of the Park District before the County proceeds. Further, he stated that
the name should remain Soldier Field. The Commissioner said he believes the legal course of action should
be followed namely, through the governmental entity that has direct responsibility for the property.
Commissioner Quigley stated that the corporate naming is nothing new and these would be benefactors.
He said he supports the resolution.
Chairman Moran referred to a June 15, 2000 article in the Daily Southtown that discusses the Chicago
Park District plan to seek corporate sponsors for parks and programs. The article stated that some
Chicago leaders say that renaming Soldier Field could help pay for its renovation and the number of
people who object to a new stadium name are such a small minority and would have no affect. He further
stated that the people who objected to changing the name of Soldier Field, both Fox News and MSNBC,
conducted polls to see whether the name should be changed. The Fox News poll was ninety-four percent
against the change and the MSNBC poll was ninety-three percent against changing the name. Also, the
Chainnan stated that the Chicago Park District has stated that a name change is not planned.

Commissioner Daley, seconded by Vice Chairman Hansen, moved to defer communication No.
237251. The motion carried.
Vice Chairman Hansen moved to adjourn the meeting, seconded by Commissioner Carr. The
motion carried.
Respectfully submitted,
COMMITTEE ON VETERANS
WILLIAM R. MORAN, Chainnan
ATTEST: SANDRA K. WILLIAMS, Secretary

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2000

Commissioner Moran, seconded by Commissioner Butler, moved that the Report of the Committee on
Veterans be approved and adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

(f)
In order to comply with certain provisions of the Internal Revenue Code of 1986, as
amended (the "Code"), the County held a public hearing on July 6, 2000 (the " Public Hearing" ),
concerning the issuance of the Bonds for which due notice was given by publi cation in the Chicago
Tribune on June 21, 2000.
(g)

The Borrower has presented the County with proposed documentation for the Bonds, as

follows:
(i)
a Placement Agreement (the " Placement Agreement"), to be entered into by and
among the County, the Partnership, and LaSalle Capital Markets, A Division of AMN AMRO
Incorporated (the "Agent''), setting forth the terms and conditions on which the County will sell
the Bonds;
(ii)
the Bond Indenture, providing for the creation of the Bonds, the terms of the
Bonds and the security for the Bonds;
the Loan Agreement, prov iding for a loan of the Bond proceeds to the Borrower
(iii)
on repayment terms scheduled to provide the County with revenues sufficient to retire the Bonds
in accordance with their tenns;
(iv)
a Preliminary Placement Memorandum (the " Preliminary Placement
Memorandum"), describing the Bonds and the security and source of payment for the Bonds;

240

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2000
(v)
a Letter of Credit, to be dated the date of issuance of the Bonds (the " Letter of
Credit") to be issued by LaSalle Bank National Association (the "Credit Entity") to provide for
the payment of the principal and interest on the Bonds and a Reimbursement Agreement pursuant
to which such Letter of Credit is to be issued (the " Reimbursement Agreement");
(vi)
a Tax Compliance Agreement to be dated the date of issuance of the Bonds (the
" Tax Agreement") by and among the County, the Trustee, the Partnership and Star Contractors
Supply, Inc., setting forth, among other matters, the reasonable expectations of the County, the
Partnership, and Star Contractors Supply, Inc. about the Bonds that are needed to establish that
the Bonds qualify as tax-exempt for federal income tax purposes; and;
(vii)
a Remarketing Agreement dated as of August I, 2000 to be entered into by the
Partnership and the Agent pursuant to which the Bonds will be remarketed (the " Remarketing
Agreement").
The financing of the Project is authorized and determined to be in the public
Section 2.
interest and in furtherance of the public purposes of the County.
Section 3.
In order to provide funds to carry out the public purposes set forth in Section 2 of
this Ordinance, the County is authorized to issue the Bonds in the aggregate principal amount of
$3,000,000.
The Bonds shall be issued as fully registered bonds without coupons; shall be dated, executed and
authenticated in the manner set forth in the Bond Indenture; shall bear interest from their date on the
unpaid principal of such Bonds at the rates per annum set forth in the Bond Indenture; shall be payable as
to principal and interest at the times and in the amounts set forth in the Bond Indenture; shall mature as
set forth in the Bond Indenture; shall be subject to redemption prior to maturity at the times, under the
circumstances, in the manner and at the redemption prices set forth in the Bond Indenture; and shall be
subject to optional and mandatory tender for purchase at the times, under the circumstances, in the
manner and at the purchase prices set forth in the Bond Indenture.
The Bonds, together with the interest payable on such Bonds, shall be limited obligations of the
County, payable solely from the payments to be made pursuant to the Loan Agreement (except to the
extent payable from Bond proceeds, the income from the temporary investment thereof and moneys
derived from payments made pursuant to instruments delivered in connection with the issuance of the
Bonds, including the Letter of Credit). The Bonds shall not constitute indebtedness or general obligations
of the County, the State of Illinois or any political subdivision of either the State of Illinois or the County
within the meaning of any constitutional provision or statutory limitation, and shall not constitute or give
rise to a pecuniary liability of the County or a charge against the general credit or taxing power of the
County, the State of Illinois or any political subdivision of either the State of lllinois or the County. No
owner of any Bond shall have the right to demand payment of the principal of, premium, if any, or
interest on any Bond from any funds raised by taxation.
Section 4.
The Bonds shall be issued in compliance with and under authority of the
provisions of this Ordinance and the Bond Indenture. The President of the Board of Commissioners and
the County Clerk are authorized for and in the name of the County to execute the Bonds. The Bonds shall
be executed on behalf of the County with the manual or facsimile signature of the President of the Board
of Commissioners and attested by the manual or facsimile signature of the County Clerk, and shall have
printed on such Bonds a facsimile of its corporate seal or impressed on such Bonds manually its corporate
seal. In case any officer who shall have signed (whether manually or in facsimile) any of the Bonds shall
cease to be such officer of the County before the Bonds have been authenticated by the Bond Trustee or

241

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2000
delivered or sold, such Bonds with the signatures to such Bonds affixed may, nevertheless, be
authenticated by the Bond Trustee, and delivered, and may be sold by the County, as though the person or
persons who signed such Bonds have remained in office. The appointment of Seaway National Bank of
Chicago, as bond trustee, under the Bond Indenture, is approved.
Section 5.
The fonns, tenns and provisions of the Loan Agreement, the Placement
Agreement, the Bond Indenture, the Tax Agreement, the Remarketing Agreement, and the Preliminary
Placement Memorandum, are in all respects approved, and the President of the Board of Commissioners
and, where indicated in such documents, the County Clerk, are authorized, empowered and directed to
execute and deliver the Loan Agreement, the Placement Agreement, the Bond Indenture and the Tax
Agreement in the name and on behalf of the County. The Loan Agreement, the Placement Agreement,
the Bond Indenture and the Tax Agreement, as executed and delivered, shall be in substantially the fonns
now before this meeting and approved, or with such changes in such forms as shall be approved by the
officers of the County executing the same, their execution of such documents to constitute conclusive
evidence of their approval of any and all changes or revisions in such fonns from the forms of the Loan
Agreement, the Placement Agreement, the Bond Indenture and the Tax Agreement now before this
meeting; and from and after the execution and delivery of the Loan Agreement, the Placement
Agreement, the Bond Indenture and the Tax Agreement, the officers, agents and employees of the County
are authorized, empowered and directed to do all such acts and things and to execute all such documents
as may be necessary to carry out the intent and accomplish the purposes of this Ordinance and to comply
with and make effective the provisions of the Loan Agreement, the Placement Agreement, the Bond
Indenture and the Tax Agreement, as executed.
Section 6.
The fonns , tenns and provisions of the Letter of Credit and the Reimbursement
Agreement substantially in the fonns presented at this meeting are in all respects approved, or with such
changes in such forms as shall be approved by the officers of the County executing the Bond Indenture,
their execution of the Bond Indenture to constitute conclusive evidence of their approval of any and all
changes or revisions to the Letter of Credit and the Reimbursement Agreement from the forms now
before this meeting.
Section 7.
The sale of the Bonds pursuant to the Placement Agreement among the County,
the Partnership and LaSalle Capital Markets, A Division of ABN AMRO Incorporated, as placement
agent, at a price equal to 100% of the principal amount of the Bonds, is authorized and approved. The
payment of a fee to the Placement Agent in the amount set forth in the Placement Agreement is hereby
approved. In connection with the sale of the Bonds, it is contemplated that the Preliminary Placement
Memorandum and a Placement Memorandum will be distributed and the County approves the distribution
of the Preliminary Placement Memorandum and a Placement Memorandum in connection with the sale of
the Bonds substantially in the fonn of the Preliminary Placement Memorandum presented at this meeting
or with such changes therein as shall be approved by the officers of the County executing the Placement
Agreement, the execution of the Placement Agreement to constitute conclusive evidence of the approval
of any and all changes or revisions to the Preliminary Placement Memorandum and the Placement
Memorandum from the fonn of the Preliminary Placement Memorandum now befo re this meeting.
Section 8.
The remarketing of the Bonds pursuant to the Remarketing Agreement is
approved. The fonn, tenns and provisions of the Remarketing Agreement substantially in the fonn
presented at this meeting are in all respects approved, or with such changes therein as shall be approved
by the officer of the County executing the Placement Agreement, the execution of the Placement
Agreement by such officer to constitute conclusive evidence of the approval of any and all changes or
revisions to the Remarketing Agreement from the fonn now before this meeting. The appointment of

Section 10.

limitation, the Internal Revenue Service Fonn 8038), as may be necessary to carry out and comply with
the provisions of the documents as executed, and to further the purposes and intent of this Ordinance.
Section I I.
The adoption and approval of this Ordinance shall constitute approval of the
Bonds by the Board of Commissioners and the President of the Board of Commissioners for purposes of
Section l 47(f) of the Code.
Section 12.
The Board of Commissioners allocate to the Bonds an amount of the County's
volume cap allocation under Section I 46 of the Code equal to the amount of the Bonds issued under the
Indenture and delivered in accordance with the Placement Agreement, provided such allocation shall not
exceed $3,000,000.
Section 13.
The County hereby elects, under Section 144(a)(4) of the Code to substitute
$10,000,000 for $ 1,000,000 in paragraph ( 1) of Section 144(a) of the Code, with respect to the Bonds.
Section 14.
All acts and doings of the officials of the County that are in confonnity with the
purposes and intent of this Ordinance and in furtherance of the issuance of the Bonds be, and the same are
in all respects, approved and confinned. The County covenants that it will take no action or fail to take
any action that would cause the Bonds to become invalid.
Section 15.
The provisions of this Ordinance are declared to be separable and if any section,
phrase or provision shall for any reason be declared by a court of competent jurisdiction to be invalid or
unenforceable, such declaration shall not affect the validity or enforceability of the remainder of the
sections, phrases and provisions of this Ordinance.
This Ordinance shall constitute complete authority for the issuance of the Bonds.
Section 16.
All ordinance, orders, and resolutions and parts of them in conflict with this Ordinance are to the extent of
such conflict repealed, and this Ordinance shall take effect and be in full force immediately upon its
adoption.
Section 17.
A copy of this Ordinance shall be filed in the office of the County Clerk and shall
be made available for public inspection in the manner required by Jaw.
Section 18.

This Ordinance shall become effective upon its passage and approval.

RESOLUTIONS

OO-R-447
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JOHN H. STROGER, JR.
PRESIDENT OF THE COOK COUNTY BOARD OF COMMISSIONERS

WHEREAS, uninsured children are not as healthy as they should be, and are less likely to receive all their
immunizations; and
WHEREAS, these children are often more likely to miss school days, which in tum prevents them from
reaching their academic potential; and
WHEREAS, 25 percent of all uninsured children do not receive necessary medical attention and are four
times more likely than insured children to have necessary medical care delayed; and
WHEREAS, uninsured children are five times more likely to use emergency room services for necessary
medical care, services which are costlier and do not ensure continuity of care; and
WHEREAS, in August of 1997 the federal Children's Health Insurance Program was enacted to provide
states with more than $24 billion over a five-year period to create their own children's health insurance
programs; and
WHEREAS, the State of Illinois created the KidCare program to provide state-sponsored health insurance
coverage to the approximately 190,000 children state-wide who are eligible yet uninsured; and
WHEREAS, a recent study by Brandeis University found that nearly 25 percent of all Cook County
children in families with incomes at or below 250 percent of the federal poverty level ($41 ,500 for a
family of four) remain uninsured; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Bureau of Health Services received an award for identifying and enrolling
the most children into the KidCare program last year, and has just recei ved a grant to hire additional
outreach workers to sign up more children this year.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners recognizes the
month of August 2000 as KidCare Month in Cook County and urges all citizens to help the State of
lllinois reach its goal of identifying and enrolling all eligible, yet uninsured children into the KidCare
program and to recognize the importance of health insurance for children to prevent and treat illnesses in
a timely, responsible manner which will in tum ensure their ability to maximize their academic, social and
athletic capabilities.
Approved and adopted this 9th day of August 2000.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DA YID ORR, County Clerk

OO-R-449
RESOLUTION

Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE TED LECHOWICZ, PRESIDENT JOHN H. STROGER, JR.,
JOHN P. DALEY AND ALLAN C. CARR, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
Co-Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JERRY BUTLER, EARLEAN COLLINS, GREGG GOSLIN,
CARL R. HANSEN, ROBERTO MALDONADO, WILLIAM R. MORAN,
JOSEPH MARIO MORENO, MIKE QUIGLEY, HERBERT T. SCHUMANN, JR.,
PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIMS, BOBBIE L. STEELE
AND CALVIN R. SUTKER, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS

WHEREAS, the Honorable Donald P. O'Connell, Chief Judge of the Circuit Court of Cook
County, was honored on July 7, 2000, by the American Bar Association with its "Award of Judicial
Excellence"; and
WHEREAS, this award recognizes Judge O'Connell 's more than 27 years of outstanding
perfonnance and extraordinary service in the Circuit Court of Cook County, the largest unified court
system in the nation (currently having 416 judges who sit in 15 divisions or districts); and
WHEREAS, during his long tenure with the Circuit Court, Judge O'Connell has served in a
variety of capacities, including Administrative Director of the Court ( 1973-1978), Presiding Judge of the
First Municipal District ( 1984-1990), Presiding Judge of the Law Division ( 1990-1994) and Chief Judge
(December 5, 1994, to the present); and
WHEREAS, as Chief Judge, Judge O'Connell has, inter a/ia, substantially reduced the backlog of
cases in the court system, instituted new initiatives to help victims of domestic abuse, and established
numerous other programs to improve the court system; and
WHEREAS, Judge O' Connell has also reformed and reorganized the juvenile court system in
Cook County to create the Juvenile Justice Division (which deals with delinquent children), the Child
Protection Section (which is dedicated to serving abused and neglected children), and the Juvenile Justice
and Child Protection Resource Section (which identifies community-based resources, devises training
programs, and recruits volunteers to help juvenile court wards); and

246

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2000
WHEREAS, since this reorganization, the juvenile court system has implemented a wide range of
options to detention and has experienced increased efficiencies in case processing, improved
communications among court agencies, increased and earlier referrals to community-based organizations,
and increased sharing of resources between community-based organizations and the court, resulting in
substantial reductions in the juvenile detention population; and
WHEREAS, under Judge O'Connell's leadership, the Cook County Juvenile Court has
established working relationships with approximately 300 community-based organizations to deliver
services to children and families; and
WHEREAS, Judge O 'Connell has also received numerous other awards and recogmt10ns,
including the Chicago Bar Association Board of Manager's " Resolution fo r Outstand ing Leadership of
the Circuit Court" (1999), the Chicagoland Chamber of Commerce's " Public Service Award for
Outstanding Achievement and Contribution to Crime Prevention and Law Enforcement" ( 1999), the
Illinois State Bar Association's " Access to Justice Award" ( 1997), the Cook County Bar Association's
"Albert C. Maule Public Service Award" ( 1997), the Illinois State Bar Association's " Board of Governors
Award" ( 1995) and Chicago Lawyer's " Person of the Year Award" (1991 ); and
WHEREAS, these many awards and the recent recognition by the American Bar Association
reflect the extraordinary achievements and contributions by Judge O'Connell and his dedication and
commitment during his many years of service on the bench; and
WHEREAS, this Body takes great pride in recognizing the accomplishments and successes of
those who have been dedicated to the service of the people of Cook County.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County
does hereby congratulate the Honorable Donald P. O 'Connell, Chief Judge of the Circuit Court of Cook
County, on his receipt of the American Bar Association's "Award of Judicial Excellence"; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be tendered to Chief
Judge O' Connell as recognition of his achievements and contributions and also spread upon the official
proceedings of this Honorable Body.
Approved and adopted this 9th day of August 2000.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAYID ORR, County Clerk

Honoring the 150th Anniversary of Leyden Township
WHEREAS, the Township of Leyden, in Cook County, Illinois, was fonned m 1850 as Monroe
Township and was renamed Leyden Township in 185 1; and

25 1

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2000

WHEREAS, Leyden Township is the third largest township in Illinois and consists of an unincorporated
area, all of Elmwood Park, Franklin Park, River Grove, Schiller Park and parts of Rosemont, Norridge,
Northlake and Park Ridge; and

WHEREAS, Leyden Township provides numerous vital services to its 89,142 residents, including
general assistance, senior and youth programs, programs for the disabled, a handyman program, tax
assistance, veterans' assistance and Pace Bus service; and

WHEREAS, Leyden Township is responsible for the maintenance of approximately thirty miles of
streets in its unincorporated area; and

WHEREAS, every year the Township staff altruistically collects and distributes food baskets to Leyden's
neediest families during the Thanksgiving and Christmas seasons; and

WHEREAS, Leyden Township's elected officials; Supervisor Bradley Stephens, Clerk Donna Geneva
Roehri, Trustees Albert Biancalana, Marilynn May, Joseph Thomas, Sr. and Gregory lgnoffo, along with
the administrators and employees of the township offices and the thousands of families who reside in
Leyden Township are a valued and respected part of the County of Cook.

NOW, THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED, that the President and the Members of the Board of
Commissioners of Cook County does hereby congratulate the Township of Leyden on their I50th
Anniversary and sincerely thank them for their contributions to our county; and

BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED that a suitable copy of this Resolution be presented to Leyden
Township as evidence of the esteem in which it is held by this Honorable Body.

OO-R-455

WHEREAS, Mario and Clara Silvestri were married on August 19, 1950 at the Church of Santa Maria in
Pofi, Province of Frosinone, in Italy; and
WHEREAS, Mario and Clara Silvestri immigrated to Brantford, Ontario, Canada in 1950 and 1956, and
to Chicago, Illinois, USA in 1962; and
WHEREAS, Mario Silvestri worked in the automotive industry, ending his career at International
Harvester, Melrose Park, Illinois in 1983; and
WHEREAS, Clara Silvestri grew up in a family in the fabrics industry and worked in the tailoring
industry, ending her career as a supervisor at Hart Shaffner & Marx, Chicago, Illinois in 1984 ; and
WHEREAS, Mario and Clara Silvestri are the devoted parents of Peter N. Silvestri and are the devoted
grandparents of Christian Peter Silvestri; and
WHEREAS, Mario and Clara Silvestri are members of a variety of community and social clubs and
organizations and are parishioners at Saint Cyprian's Church in River Grove, lllinois; and
WHEREAS, Mario and Clara Silvestri will celebrate with friends and family their 50th Wedding
Anniversary at Elmcrest Banquets, Elmwood Park, Illinois on Sunday, August 13, 2000.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners does
hereby congratulate Mario and Clara Silvestri on their long and happy life together; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be spread upon the official
proceedings of this Honorable Body and that a copy of same be tendered to Mario and Clara Silvestri in
recognition of their 50th Wedding Anniversary.

WHEREAS, Sunday, September 10, 2000, the North Riverside Police Benevolent Association, Unit 73 is
honoring Sergeant John O' Rourke on his retirement; and
WHEREAS, Sergeant O ' Rourke embarked on a career in law enforcement with the North Riverside
Police Department on June 1, 1969 and seven years later, in 1976 was promoted to the rank of Sergeant;
and
WHEREAS, during his thirty-one years of service with the North Riverside Police Department, Sergeant
O' Rourke has gained recognition for hi s accomplishments by receiving the Prestig ious Illinois Police
Association Life Saving Award; seven commendatory letters; one unit citation, one honorable mention
and many personal letters of appreciation; and
WHEREAS, in 1979 Sergeant O' Rourke was elected President of the Police Benevolent Protective
Association where in 1985 he aided in establishing the first collective bargaining agreement and since its
inception has remained at the forefront in every contract negotiation; and
WHEREAS, the "John O ' Rourke Award", was established as a tribute to Sergeant O ' Rourke for his
unswerving dedication to the collective bargaining movement in police work. The award is presented
annually to an officer or officers for their outstanding performance concerning collective bargaining; and

255

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2000
WHEREAS, Sergeant O'Rourke volunteered his time and support to the Ed Schwartz Food Drive and
helped collect thousands of pounds of food for the homeless and hungry; he instituted the not-for-profit
Easter Egg Hunt and free hot dog lunch for the community for the past nineteen years; and
WHEREAS, Sergeant O' Rourke and Sandra, his wife of thirty-seven years, have reared fi ve children,
John Jr., Susan, Timothy, Theresa and Kevin and are looking forward to a well earned and deserved
retirement; and
WHEREAS, this Body takes great pride in recognizing those citizens of this County, who are noted for
their achievements and contributions.
NOW THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED , that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County does
hereby congratulate Sergeant O ' Rourke for his thirty-one years of service to law enforcement, his
dedication and commitment to his department, his community and his fellow officers and take this
opportunity to wish him many years of health and happiness during his retirement.

WHEREAS, Dr. Sheldon Berger was a prominent endocrinologist, a professor of medicine at
Northwestern Memorial Hospital. He was a pioneer in researching diabetes and hyperglycemia, was the
director of the Chicago Center of Clinical Research and ran a private practice for almost 30 years, and
WHEREAS, Dr. Sheldon Berger's son Norman described his father as, "The consummate teacher who
inspired his colleagues. His work and life touched so many people. He was dedicated to his research.",
and

266

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2000
WHEREAS, Dr. Sheldon Berger began his medical career at Michael Reese Hospital as a leading
researcher of radioisotopes for the diagnosis of thyroid disease. He moved to Evanston Hospital to direct
the research laboratory in 1969, and
WHEREAS, Dr. Sheldon Berger was instrumental in the development of new drugs to treat osteoporosis
and diabetes, and he had been working on projects for inhaled insulin to treat diabetes, and
WHEREAS, Dr. Michael Davidson, president of the Chicago Center of Clinical Research stated, "His
intellect, compassion, integrity and thirst for knowledge made Shelly Berger the doctor's doctor. He was
an inspiration, a friend and mentor to countless individuals who have pursued medical careers.", now

WHEREAS, the alumni of New Trier High School include Charles Percy, Rahm Emanuel, Donald
Rumsfeld, Scott Turow, Charlton Heston and Christie Hefner among others, and
WHEREAS, New Trier High School, which opened in 1901 with 76 students, today enrolls 3,400
students. Enrollment peaked in 1972, when the east and west campuses were merged with 6,558 students.
The west campus closed in 1981 , but is reopening for freshmen in 2001 , and
WHEREAS, visiting alumni will find a campus where some things never change. Since the 1920s, New
Trier has maintained an unusual advisory system in which teachers are assigned to meet regularly and
counsel the same 25 students throughout their four years. Fortunately, some things have changed with the
use of air conditioners to keep the school cool during wann weather, and
WHEREAS, the students of New Trier have the same disciplined work ethic that enabled many alumni
from prior years to succeed. Students carry heavy workloads and take advanced placement classes to
compete for s pots at the nation's most prestigious colleges, and

volunteer work for charities and community groups. Even though many were children of privilege, they

State of Illinois and their country, now
THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners does hereby
congratulate New Trier High School on its' centennial anniversary and hopes that during the next 100
years New Trier continues its tradition of excellence, and

produce festival plays at North Shore Congregation Israel in Glencoe for 20 years, and
WHEREAS, Dorothy Sigel was the first president of the North Shore Chapter of Hadassah in the early

ABEYELEN
WHEREAS, Abe Y elen was the loving husband of Sara, and
WHEREAS, Abe Y elen was the adoring father of Esther, Adina and Arie, and
WHEREAS, Abe Yelen was the affectionate grandfather of Ron, Dana, Tracey, James, Leor, Yoni and
Ben, and
WHEREAS, Abe Yelen was a war prisoner of the Gennans and a political prisoner in the Soviet Union
before he was twenty-five years old. He recounted these experiences on fi lm in a Steven Spielberg
project, and
WHEREAS, according to his family, the chief legacy of Abe Yelen was his call to care for others. Abe's
belief was, " While we are here, we have to do things for the community", and
WHEREAS, Abe Yelen was a veteran of the Polish and Israeli Anny, and
WHEREAS, Abe Yelen was from a family of seven children in a small Polish town when he was drafted
into the Polish anny in 1939, a few months before Gennany invaded. After the Polish anny was defeated,
he was captured and taken as a prisoner of war and sent to Gennany, and
WHEREAS, Abe Yelen was later released and headed back to Poland. Along the way, he saw that Jews
were being rounded up and decided to persuade his family to leave. His family resisted his pleas, and he
made his way without them across the Russian border, and
WHEREAS, Abe Yelen was arrested by the Russians and shipped off to a camp in Siberia where he
spent two years as a political prisoner. After Gennany invaded Russia, Abe was freed and recruited to
fight with a free Polish anny fonned under British command, and

273

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2000

WHEREAS, when the anny, bound to fight in Africa, stopped in Palestine, Abe Y elen stayed. He had no
contact with his family for more than one year. He eventually learned his immediate family perished in
the Nazi Holocaust. He learned he had a first cousin in Chicago and came to Chicago in 1960 and has
resided in the United States since, and
WHEREAS, Abe Yelen found others from his native area as well in the Midwest Chenstochower Society
here, and became active in the group, and
WHEREAS, Abe Y elen brought his family to Chicago by 1961. He owned a unifonn business,
Economic Unifonn Manufacturing. The company made clothing for firefighters, security guards,
civilians and Chicago Police and he built a thriving business, now
THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners does hereby offer
its deepest condolences and most heartfelt sympathy to the family of Abe Yelen and joins them in sorrow
at this time of loss, and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that this text be spread upon the official proceedings of this Honorable
Body and a copy of same be tendered to the family of Abe Yel en.
Approved and adopted this 9th day of August 2000.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAVID ORR, County Clerk

WHEREAS, the National Association of Hispanic Journalists (NAHJ) created the Professional
Journalism Awards Contest to honor the finest Latino professionals in broadcast, photojournalism and
print; and

278

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2000
WHEREAS, Jorge Luis Mota a reporter for Exito newspaper, the Chicago Tribune's Spanish
weekly, has been named the 2000 recipient of the prestigious Guillermo Martinez-Marquez Award, the
NAHJ's highest accolade among all media categories; and
WHEREAS, Mota faced formidable competition from representatives of companies such as The
New York Times, CNN and Univision; and
WHEREAS, Mota was honored for his article, "Negligencia? Victimas de Cancer Acusan a una
Fabrica", portraying the struggle of immigrants pursuing a better life in the United States while working
in a factory; and
WHEREAS, following his strong desire to live in freedom, Mota arrived in the U.S. from Cuba
in 1996 after surviving a treacherous twelve day raft journey; and
WHEREAS, for one and a half years, Mota lived in the Guatanamo Bay Naval Base refugee
camp with 34,000 other Cuban refugees; and
WHEREAS, Mota spent his time at the camp learning English and bettering the lives of his
fellow refugees by starting a vocational school using recycled computers from the Naval Base dump for
classroom instruction. By the end of his stay at the camp, Mota had enrolled over 2,000 refugee students
in the school; and
WHEREAS, as Exito 's community reporter, Mota brings a deep understanding of human
struggle and survival, investigating and reporting on various topics concerning Latinos in the Chicagoland
area, including politics, labor issues, immigration and education; and
WHEREAS, Mota is worthy of our great admiration and respect for winning a coveted
Guillermo Martinez-Marquez Award, which is bestowed upon him by his colleagues in the national
Latino journalism community.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board President and the
Members of the Board of Commissioners take this opportunity on behalf of the people of Cook County to
recognize and honor Jorge Luis Mota on his admirable journalistic achievements; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a copy of this Resolution be spread upon the official
proceedings of the Board of Commissioners of Cook County, and that a copy thereof be transmitted as a
testimonial of the high esteem and appreciation in which Jorge Luis Mota is regarded by the Members of
the Board of Commissioners of Cook County.

Approved and adopted this 9th day of August 2000.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAVID ORR, County Clerk

Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE GREGG GOSLIN, COUNTY COMMISSIONER
Co Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JOHN H. STROGER, JR., PRESIDENT, JERRY BUTLER,
ALLAN C. CARR, EARLEAN COLLINS, JOHN P. DALEY,
CARL R. HANSEN, TED LECHOWICZ, ROBERTO MALDONADO,
WILLIAM R. MORAN, JOSEPH MARIO MORENO, MIKE QUIGLEY,
HERBERT T. SCHUMANN, JR., PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIMS,
BOBBIE L. STEELE AND CALVIN R. SUTKER,
COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
Support of the Extension of Route 53 from
Lake-Cook Road to State Route 120 and Eastward to Interstate 94
WHEREAS, Cook County has long supported regional highway planning; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Highway Department has combined their resources with regional
transportation providers and planners to take a comprehensive look at transportation as part of the Lake
County Transportation Improvement Project (LCTIP); and
WHEREAS, hundreds of thousands of vehicle trips are made each day between Cook County
and Lake County; and
WHEREAS, the current situation with IL 53 ending at Lake-Cook Road is causing motorists to
divert onto other roadways including County highways; and
WHEREAS, the resulting congestion is also causing traffic to spill over onto local roadways in
the Villages of Palatine, Arlington Heights, Wheeling and Buffalo Grove; and
WHEREAS, this congestion contributes to high accident rates, most notable at the intersections
of Rand and Dundee, and Rand and Lake Cook Roads, which were recently listed as the two most
dangerous intersections in Illinois; and
WHEREAS, the LCTIP has undertaken a comprehensive study and identified the extension of IL
53 as a finalist option based upon its ability to improve travel for motorists; and
WHEREAS, the extension ofIL 53 will reduce congestion on existing roadways; and
WHEREAS, the LCTlP's analysis has shown that the alternatives to IL 53 have comparable
impacts to the environment and higher costs; and
WHEREAS, public and agency input will be an essential part of the decision making process.

281

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2000
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners
supports the extension ofIL 53 from its present tenninus to fL 120 and eastward to 1-94 as recommended
in the CATS 20 I 0 and 2020 regional transportation plans; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED , that the text of this Resolution be spread upon the official
record of this Honorable Body, and that a suitable copy be provided to the Cook County Highway
Department, the Lake County Division of Transportation, the Illinois Department of Transportation, the
Lake County Transportation Improvement Project, and the Villages of Palatine, Arlington Heights,
Wheeling, Buffalo Grove, Barrington and Palatine and Wheeling Townships.

Approved and adopted this 9th day of August 2000.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAYID ORR, County Clerk
Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commissioner Moreno, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.
